Therefore, if condition in equation 93 holds, then event A𝐴A occurs and following the same argument as in the proof of Proposition 5 the proof is complete.

∎

B. Infinite hypothesis class: Lipschitz continuous functions

In this section, we seek to extend Proposition 2 and 4 to infinite hypothesis class of Lipschitz continuous functions that we formally define next.Define a map Φ:𝒫×𝒳→ℝ:Φ→𝒫𝒳ℝ\Phi:\mathcal{P}\times\mathcal{X}\rightarrow\mathbb{R}from the parameter space 𝒫𝒫\mathcal{P} and the feature space 𝒳𝒳\mathcal{X} to reals. Each p∈𝒫𝑝𝒫p\in\mathcal{P} is a possible choice for the representation Φ​(p,⋅)Φ𝑝⋅\Phi(p,\cdot). Consider neural networks as an example, 𝒫𝒫\mathcal{P} represents the set of the values the weights of the network can take.

From Assumption 13 derive the conditions in Assumption 3 and Assumption 14Φ:𝒫×𝒳→ℝ:Φ→𝒫𝒳ℝ\Phi:\mathcal{P}\times\mathcal{X}\rightarrow\mathbb{R} is a continuous function defined over closed and bounded domain 𝒫×𝒳𝒫𝒳\mathcal{P}\times\mathcal{X} (domain is compact) and as a result ΦΦ\Phi is bounded say by M𝑀M.

Consider square loss ℓ​(Φ​(p,X),Y)=(Y−Φ​(p,X))2≤(M+K)2ℓΦ𝑝𝑋𝑌superscript𝑌Φ𝑝𝑋2superscript𝑀𝐾2\ell(\Phi(p,X),Y)=(Y-\Phi(p,X))^{2}\leq(M+K)^{2}. Hence, there exists an L𝐿L such that|ℓ​(Φ​(⋅),⋅)|≤L≤(M+K)2ℓΦ⋅⋅𝐿superscript𝑀𝐾2|\ell(\Phi(\cdot),\cdot)|\leq L\leq(M+K)^{2}.

∂ℓ(w.Φ(⋅),⋅)∂w|w=1.0\frac{\partial\ell(w.\Phi(\cdot),\cdot)}{\partial w}\Big{|}_{w=1.0} is bounded: |∂ℓ(w.Φ(⋅),⋅)∂w|w=1.0|=|(Y−Φ(p,X))Φ(p,X)|≤(K+M)M\Big{|}\frac{\partial\ell(w.\Phi(\cdot),\cdot)}{\partial w}\Big{|}_{w=1.0}\Big{|}=|(Y-\Phi(p,X))\Phi(p,X)|\leq(K+M)M. C. EIRM: Sample complexity with no distributional assumptions

In this section, we discuss the extension of Proposition 2 to the infinite hypothesis class case.Consider the problem in equation 6 and replace the ϵitalic-ϵ\epsilon with ϵ+κitalic-ϵ𝜅\epsilon+\kappa. Define distance between the two sets 𝒮𝖨𝖵​(ϵ)superscript𝒮𝖨𝖵italic-ϵ\mathcal{S}^{\mathsf{IV}}(\epsilon) and its approximation 𝒮𝖨𝖵​(ϵ+κ)superscript𝒮𝖨𝖵italic-ϵ𝜅\mathcal{S}^{\mathsf{IV}}(\epsilon+\kappa) as follows

𝖽𝗂𝗌​(κ)=maxg∈𝒮𝖨𝖵​(ϵ+κ)⁡minh∈𝒮𝖨𝖵​(ϵ)⁡𝖽​(g,h)𝖽𝗂𝗌𝜅subscript𝑔superscript𝒮𝖨𝖵italic-ϵ𝜅subscriptℎsuperscript𝒮𝖨𝖵italic-ϵ𝖽𝑔ℎ\mathsf{dis}(\kappa)=\max_{g\in\mathcal{S}^{\mathsf{IV}}(\epsilon+\kappa)}\min_{h\in\mathcal{S}^{\mathsf{IV}}(\epsilon)}\mathsf{d}(g,h)(100)

where 𝖽​(g,h)𝖽𝑔ℎ\mathsf{d}(g,h) is some metric that measures the distance between functions g𝑔g and hℎh. Observe that if a≤b𝑎𝑏a\leq b, 𝖽𝗂𝗌​(a)≤𝖽𝗂𝗌​(b)𝖽𝗂𝗌𝑎𝖽𝗂𝗌𝑏\mathsf{dis}(a)\leq\mathsf{dis}(b).

DefineD∗=max⁡{32​L2ν2​[k​log⁡(16​C​P​kν)+log⁡(2δ)],8​L′⁣4κ2​[k​log⁡(8​C′​P​kκ)+log⁡(2δ)]}superscript𝐷32superscript𝐿2superscript𝜈2delimited-[]𝑘16𝐶𝑃𝑘𝜈2𝛿8superscript𝐿′4superscript𝜅2delimited-[]𝑘8superscript𝐶′𝑃𝑘𝜅2𝛿D^{*}=\max\Big{\{}\frac{32L^{2}}{\nu^{2}}\Big{[}k\log\Big{(}\frac{16C\sqrt{Pk}}{\nu}\Big{)}+\log\Big{(}\frac{2}{\delta}\Big{)}\Big{]},\frac{8L^{\prime 4}}{\kappa^{2}}\Big{[}k\log\Big{(}\frac{8C^{\prime}\sqrt{Pk}}{\kappa}\Big{)}+\log\Big{(}\frac{2}{\delta}\Big{)}\Big{]}\Big{\}}

We divide the proof in two parts.

Define an event A𝐴A: {D~:∀p∈𝒫,|R′​(Φ​(p,⋅))−R^′​(Φ​(p,⋅))|≤κ}conditional-set~𝐷formulae-sequencefor-all𝑝𝒫superscript𝑅′Φ𝑝⋅superscript^𝑅′Φ𝑝⋅𝜅\{\tilde{D}:\forall p\in\mathcal{P},|R^{{}^{\prime}}(\Phi(p,\cdot))-\hat{R}^{{}^{\prime}}(\Phi(p,\cdot))|\leq\kappa\}.

R′​(Φ​(p,⋅))≤ϵ⟹R′​(Φ​(p,⋅))−R^′​(Φ​(p,⋅))+R^′​(Φ​(p,⋅))≤ϵ⟹R^′​(Φ​(p,⋅))≤ϵ+|R′​(Φ​(p,⋅))−R^′​(Φ​(p,⋅))|⟹R^′​(Φ​(p,⋅))≤ϵ+κsuperscript𝑅′Φ𝑝⋅italic-ϵsuperscript𝑅′Φ𝑝⋅superscript^𝑅′Φ𝑝⋅superscript^𝑅′Φ𝑝⋅italic-ϵsuperscript^𝑅′Φ𝑝⋅italic-ϵsuperscript𝑅′Φ𝑝⋅superscript^𝑅′Φ𝑝⋅superscript^𝑅′Φ𝑝⋅italic-ϵ𝜅\begin{split}&R^{{}^{\prime}}(\Phi(p,\cdot))\leq\epsilon\implies R^{{}^{\prime}}(\Phi(p,\cdot))-\hat{R}^{{}^{\prime}}(\Phi(p,\cdot))+\hat{R}^{{}^{\prime}}(\Phi(p,\cdot))\leq\epsilon\implies\\&\hat{R}^{{}^{\prime}}(\Phi(p,\cdot))\leq\epsilon+|R^{{}^{\prime}}(\Phi(p,\cdot))-\hat{R}^{{}^{\prime}}(\Phi(p,\cdot))|\implies\hat{R}^{{}^{\prime}}(\Phi(p,\cdot))\leq\epsilon+\kappa\\\end{split}(101)

We substitute Φ​(p∗,⋅)Φsuperscript𝑝⋅\Phi(p^{*},\cdot) as Φ∗superscriptΦ\Phi^{*} and Φ​(p^,⋅)Φ^𝑝⋅\Phi(\hat{p},\cdot) as Φ^^Φ\hat{\Phi} and this completes the proof.∎

∎

In the main body of the manuscript, we focused on regression (square-loss). In this section, we discuss the results that can be extended to binary classification (cross-entropy) loss. We will not go in the order in which the results were introduced in the manuscript but in an order that makes for easier exposition for the classification case.

We begin by showing how to extend Proposition 4 to binary classification (cross-entropy).Recall that the entropy of a distribution ℙXsubscriptℙ𝑋\mathbb{P}_{X} is H​(ℙ)=−𝔼ℙ​[log⁡(d​ℙ)]𝐻ℙsubscript𝔼ℙdelimited-[]𝑑ℙH(\mathbb{P})=-\mathbb{E}_{\mathbb{P}}\big{[}\log(d\mathbb{P})\big{]}. Recall that the cross entropy of ℚℚ\mathbb{Q} relative to ℙℙ\mathbb{P} is H​(ℙ,ℚ)=−𝔼ℙ​[log⁡(d​ℚ)]=H​(P)+𝖪𝖫​(d​ℙ∥d​ℚ)𝐻ℙℚsubscript𝔼ℙdelimited-[]𝑑ℚ𝐻𝑃𝖪𝖫conditional𝑑ℙ𝑑ℚH(\mathbb{P},\mathbb{Q})=-\mathbb{E}_{\mathbb{P}}\big{[}\log(d\mathbb{Q})\big{]}=H(P)+\mathsf{KL}(d\mathbb{P}\|d\mathbb{Q}).The cross entropy loss ℓℓ\ell for binary classification when using a predictor f:𝒳→[0,1]:𝑓→𝒳01f:\mathcal{X}\rightarrow[0,1] (f​(Xe)𝑓superscript𝑋𝑒f(X^{e}) is the probability of label 111 conditional on Xesuperscript𝑋𝑒X^{e}) is given as ℓ​(f​(Xe),Ye)=Ye​log⁡(f​(Xe))+(1−Ye)​log⁡(1−f​(Xe))ℓ𝑓superscript𝑋𝑒superscript𝑌𝑒superscript𝑌𝑒𝑓superscript𝑋𝑒1superscript𝑌𝑒1𝑓superscript𝑋𝑒\ell\big{(}f(X^{e}),Y^{e}\big{)}=Y^{e}\log\big{(}f(X^{e})\big{)}+(1-Y^{e})\log\big{(}1-f(X^{e})\big{)}. For the discussion below ℚ​(Ye|Xe)ℚconditionalsuperscript𝑌𝑒superscript𝑋𝑒\mathbb{Q}(Y^{e}|X^{e}) is defined in terms of f𝑓f as follows ℚ​(Ye=1|Xe)=f​(Xe)ℚsuperscript𝑌𝑒conditional1superscript𝑋𝑒𝑓superscript𝑋𝑒\mathbb{Q}(Y^{e}=1|X^{e})=f(X^{e}) (ℚ​(Ye=0|Xe)=1−f​(Xe))ℚsuperscript𝑌𝑒conditional0superscript𝑋𝑒1𝑓superscript𝑋𝑒\big{(}\mathbb{Q}(Y^{e}=0|X^{e})=1-f(X^{e})\big{)}.Re​(f)=𝔼e​[ℓ​(Ye,f​(Xe))]=𝔼e​[Ye​log⁡(f​(Xe))+(1−Ye)​log⁡(1−f​(Xe))]=𝔼e​[𝔼e​[Ye|Xe]​log⁡(f​(Xe))+(1−𝔼​[Ye|Xe])​log⁡(1−f​(Xe))]=𝔼e​[ℙ​(Ye=1|Xe)​log⁡(f​(Xe))+ℙ​(Ye=0|Xe)​log⁡(1−f​(Xe))]=𝔼e​[H​(ℙ​(Ye|Xe),ℚ​(Ye|Xe))]=𝔼e[H(ℙ(Ye|Xe))+𝖪𝖫(ℙ(Ye|Xe)∥ℚ(Ye|Xe)]=𝔼e[H(ℙ(Ye|Xe))]+𝔼e[𝖪𝖫(ℙ(Ye|Xe)∥ℚ(Ye|Xe)]\begin{split}R^{e}(f)&=\mathbb{E}^{e}\big{[}\ell(Y^{e},f\big{(}X^{e}\big{)})\big{]}\\&=\mathbb{E}^{e}\Big{[}Y^{e}\log\big{(}f(X^{e}\big{)}\big{)}+(1-Y^{e})\log\big{(}1-f\big{(}X^{e}\big{)}\big{)}\Big{]}\\&=\mathbb{E}^{e}\Big{[}\mathbb{E}^{e}\big{[}Y^{e}|X^{e}\big{]}\log\big{(}f\big{(}X^{e}\big{)}\big{)}+\big{(}1-\mathbb{E}\big{[}Y^{e}|X^{e}\big{]}\big{)}\log\big{(}1-f\big{(}X^{e}\big{)}\big{)}\Big{]}\\&=\mathbb{E}^{e}\Big{[}\mathbb{P}(Y^{e}=1|X^{e})\log\big{(}f\big{(}X^{e}\big{)}\big{)}+\mathbb{P}(Y^{e}=0|X^{e})\log\big{(}1-f\big{(}X^{e}\big{)}\big{)}\Big{]}\\&=\mathbb{E}^{e}\Big{[}H\big{(}\mathbb{P}(Y^{e}|X^{e}),\mathbb{Q}(Y^{e}|X^{e})\big{)}\Big{]}\\&=\mathbb{E}^{e}\big{[}H\big{(}\mathbb{P}(Y^{e}|X^{e})\big{)}+\mathsf{KL}\big{(}\mathbb{P}(Y^{e}|X^{e})\|\mathbb{Q}(Y^{e}|X^{e}\big{)}\big{]}\\&=\mathbb{E}^{e}\Big{[}H\big{(}\mathbb{P}(Y^{e}|X^{e})\big{)}\Big{]}+\mathbb{E}^{e}\Big{[}\mathsf{KL}\big{(}\mathbb{P}(Y^{e}|X^{e})\|\mathbb{Q}(Y^{e}|X^{e}\big{)}\Big{]}\end{split}(127)

From the above it is clear that ℚ​(Ye|Xe)=ℙ​(Ye|Xe)ℚconditionalsuperscript𝑌𝑒superscript𝑋𝑒ℙconditionalsuperscript𝑌𝑒superscript𝑋𝑒\mathbb{Q}(Y^{e}|X^{e}\big{)}=\mathbb{P}(Y^{e}|X^{e}\big{)} minimizes the risk in an individual environment.

Observe that in the binary-classification setting the above assumption amounts to equating the conditional probabilities ℙ​(Ye|Xe)ℙconditionalsuperscript𝑌𝑒superscript𝑋𝑒\mathbb{P}(Y^{e}|X^{e}) and ℙ​(Yo|Xo)ℙconditionalsuperscript𝑌𝑜superscript𝑋𝑜\mathbb{P}(Y^{o}|X^{o}).

Recall that map m𝑚m (from equation 2) simplifies to ∀x∈𝒳for-all𝑥𝒳\forall x\in\mathcal{X}m​(x)=𝔼e​[Ye|Xe=x]=ℙ​(Ye=1|Xe=x)𝑚𝑥superscript𝔼𝑒delimited-[]conditionalsuperscript𝑌𝑒superscript𝑋𝑒𝑥ℙsuperscript𝑌𝑒conditional1superscript𝑋𝑒𝑥m(x)=\mathbb{E}^{e}[Y^{e}|X^{e}=x]=\mathbb{P}(Y^{e}=1|X^{e}=x)(128)

If Assumption 16 holds, then from cross-entropy decomposition in equation 127 it is clear that m𝑚m solves the OOD problem (as it is optimal w.r.t each environment). It is also the unique minimizer. We can justify it based on the same argument presented in equation 55. Suppose there was another optimizer which was different from m𝑚m over a set with a non-zero measure. Over such a set the the KL divergence term inside equation 127 will be greater than zero, thus making the second term in equation 127 positive thus contradicting the optimality. This shows m𝑚m is the unique optimizer. The rest of the arguments presented in the proof of Proposition 4 carry over to this case. Therefore, Proposition 4 extends to the cross-entropy loss.

Note that Proposition 2’s proof was agnostic to loss type and only used boundedness, which holds for both cross-entropy as long as the probability output are in the strict interior of [0,1]01[0,1] defined by [𝗉𝗆𝗂𝗇,𝗉𝗆𝖺𝗑]⊂[0,1]subscript𝗉𝗆𝗂𝗇subscript𝗉𝗆𝖺𝗑01[\mathsf{p}_{\mathsf{min}},\mathsf{p}_{\mathsf{max}}]\subset[0,1]. We could not generalize Proposition 5 to cross-entropy loss and that is left as future work.

Next, we move to showing how Proposition 1 can be generalized to binary classification.

This completes the extension of Proposition 1 to cross-entropy.

Consider the model in Assumption 5. For each environment e∈ℰt​r𝑒subscriptℰ𝑡𝑟e\in\mathcal{E}_{tr}, define a vector ρe=𝔼e​[εe​Xe]superscript𝜌𝑒superscript𝔼𝑒delimited-[]superscript𝜀𝑒superscript𝑋𝑒\rho^{e}=\mathbb{E}^{e}\big{[}\varepsilon^{e}X^{e}\big{]}. Define a vector π¯=[π1,…,π|ℰt​r|]¯𝜋superscript𝜋1…superscript𝜋subscriptℰ𝑡𝑟\bar{\pi}=[\pi^{1},\dots,\pi^{|\mathcal{E}_{tr}|}], where recall from Assumption 5 πosuperscript𝜋𝑜\pi^{o} is probability a point comes from environment o𝑜o.

Consider the case when ERM has access to infinite data, i.e., we are solving the expected risk minimization problem stated as minΦ∈ℋΦ⁡R​(Φ)subscriptΦsubscriptℋΦ𝑅Φ\min_{\Phi\in\mathcal{H}_{\Phi}}R(\Phi). As a result a uniform random draw from this set of probablity distributions would have zero probability of satisfying ρ¯​π¯=0¯𝜌¯𝜋0\bar{\rho}\bar{\pi}=0. Therefore, 𝒮~𝖳​γsuperscript~𝒮𝖳𝛾\tilde{\mathcal{S}}^{\mathsf{T}}\gamma is not the optimal solution to ERM and thus the solution of ERM would be biased away from 𝒮~𝖳​γsuperscript~𝒮𝖳𝛾\tilde{\mathcal{S}}^{\mathsf{T}}\gamma.

∎

In Proposition 5, we had assumed Assumptions 5, 6, 7 hold. If we also assume that rank of ρ¯¯𝜌\bar{\rho} is at least one, the Proposition 5 continues to hold. If for at least one e∈ℰt​r𝑒subscriptℰ𝑡𝑟e\in\mathcal{E}_{tr}, 𝔼e​[εe​Xe]superscript𝔼𝑒delimited-[]superscript𝜀𝑒superscript𝑋𝑒\mathbb{E}^{e}\big{[}\varepsilon^{e}X^{e}\big{]} is non-zero, then the rank of ρ¯¯𝜌\bar{\rho} is at least one. From proof of Theorem 10 in [Arjovsky et al., 2019], linear general position continues to hold except over a set of covariance matrices with measure zero even when one of the 𝔼e​[εe​Xe]superscript𝔼𝑒delimited-[]superscript𝜀𝑒superscript𝑋𝑒\mathbb{E}^{e}\big{[}\varepsilon^{e}X^{e}\big{]} is non-zero.

Also, in the above Proposition 17, we only required that rank of ρ¯¯𝜌\bar{\rho} is at least one. However, if we make the additional assumptions 5, 6, 7, the result of the above Proposition continues to hold. Therefore, if Assumption 5, 6, 7 hold and rank of ρ¯¯𝜌\bar{\rho} is at least one, then ERM is asymptotically biased and IRM can be within ϵitalic-ϵ\sqrt{\epsilon} neighborhood of the ideal solution with the sample complexity shown in Proposition 5.
